  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7cdadbef-33f7-4f6f-bd5a-09372d4d22a9'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText15596960747092682938" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>A tale of twelve princesses doomed to dance until dawn…</i>
</b><br /><br />Galen is a young soldier returning from war; Rose is one of twelve princesses condemned to dance each night for the King Under Stone. Together Galen and Rose will search for a way to break the curse that forces the princesses to dance at the midnight balls. All they need is one invisibility cloak, a black wool chain knit with enchanted silver needles, and that most critical ingredient of all—true love—to conquer their foes in the dark halls below. But malevolent forces are working against them above ground as well, and as cruel as the King Under Stone has seemed, his wrath is mere irritation compared to the evil that awaits Galen and Rose in the brighter world above. <br /><br />Captivating from start to finish, Jessica Day George’s take on the Grimms’ tale <i>The Twelve Dancing Princesses </i>demonstrates yet again her mastery at spinning something entirely fresh out of a story you thought you knew.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">yes, each of the main characters are sisters. There is an overarching plot, so the books should be read in this order: 'Princess of the Midnight Ball'<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">yes, each of the main characters are sisters. There is an overarching plot, so the books should be read in this order: 'Princess of the Midnight Ball' first, 'Princess of Glass' second, and 'Princess of the Silver Woods' last.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_50819240" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50819240" />
    <a title="Amber" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1026285-amber"><img alt="Amber" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222894636p2/1026285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50819240?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/1026285-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50819240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11453592403707518554">This story was lacking in too many elements to be enjoyable for me. The characters were so underdeveloped that the weren't likable- the writing didn't make me love the hero or hate the villain. The romance lacked passion and believability. I couldn't ever figure out what the hero and heroine saw in each other, and why the hero would go to such lengths to save the heroine. And the plot was so predicable- I never wondered whether or not the princesses would be saved in the end, and the ending wasn</span>
  <span id="freeText11453592403707518554" style="display:none">This story was lacking in too many elements to be enjoyable for me. The characters were so underdeveloped that the weren't likable- the writing didn't make me love the hero or hate the villain. The romance lacked passion and believability. I couldn't ever figure out what the hero and heroine saw in each other, and why the hero would go to such lengths to save the heroine. And the plot was so predicable- I never wondered whether or not the princesses would be saved in the end, and the ending wasn't suspenseful at all. I would have liked more detail and description in this story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11453592403707518554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_835766213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/835766213" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/835766213?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=squeaky-clean-romance">squeaky-clean-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=too-juvenile-for-me">too-juvenile-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=princes-and-princesses">princes-and-princesses</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer835766213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12516122910134107341">Final review, first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>: <br/><br/>The malevolent King Under Stone cuts not one deal, but two, with the queen of the country of Westfalin: first, that she will be able to have children; second, that Westfalin will be victorious in its battles against other countries. In return, the human queen agrees to spend one night per week dancing with the King Under Stone in his underground kingdom. But the once-human king has an agenda, and supernatural beings have a way of twisting their a</span>
  <span id="freeText12516122910134107341" style="display:none">Final review, first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>: <br /><br />The malevolent King Under Stone cuts not one deal, but two, with the queen of the country of Westfalin: first, that she will be able to have children; second, that Westfalin will be victorious in its battles against other countries. In return, the human queen agrees to spend one night per week dancing with the King Under Stone in his underground kingdom. But the once-human king has an agenda, and supernatural beings have a way of twisting their agreements to find loopholes. The Westfalin queen bears no sons, but has twelve daughters ― not coincidentally, matching the number of half-human sons of the King Under Stone, who plans for his sons to have mortal wives and thus break the king out of his underground bondage.<br /><br />When the queen dies before fulfilling her bargain, the King Under Stone forces her twelve daughters to finish the contract by secretly coming down to his kingdom and dancing with his dark sons. In fact, he has no intention of releasing them, and is slowly binding the girls with his magic to his kingdom, as well as preventing them from telling anyone what is happening to them. Their frantic father, the King of Westfalin, begs for help from neighboring royalty and nobility, but each young man who tries to find out why the princesses are exhausted and have worn-out dancing slippers falls asleep, fails to solve the puzzle … and then mysteriously dies. But a polite young soldier named Galen, returning from Westfalin’s latest war, is kind to an old woman who then gifts him with an invisibility cloak and some very good advice.<br /><br />This young adult retelling of “The Twelve Dancing Princesses” recreates their story with a few minor twists, such as the scheming role of the King Under Stone (who is the person responsible for the young men’s deaths, not the girls’ father), the fuller development of a relationship between the oldest princess and the soldier, and Galen’s unusual aptitude for knitting (apparently it’s very useful for soldiers to be able to knit socks), which will eventually play a role in the resolution of the mystery. But in general Jessica Day George follows the traditional plotline, so the surprises are relatively mild for any reader familiar with the original story.<br /><br />All twelve princesses are named after flowers ― Rose, Lily, Jonquil, Hyacinth, Violet and so forth. Who knew there were so many flower names for girls? I wasn’t able to keep any of them straight except for the two eldest, Rose and Lily, and the priggish Hyacinth. Still, with twelve sisters, this likely would have been an issue for me no matter what they were named.<br /><br />I found <i>Princess of the Midnight Ball</i> pleasant reading but not memorable. In fairness, though, this middle grade/young adult novel seems to be aimed at a fairly young audience, who may not be familiar with the original fairy tale and who will be more apt to be enchanted by the magical world George creates and the budding romance between Galen and the oldest princess, Rose. For readers who enjoy young adult fairy tale retellings but are looking for a greater amount of depth and more twists on the original twelve dancing princesses tale, I recommend Juliet Marillier’s Romanian-based retelling, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13929.Wildwood_Dancing__Wildwood___1_" title="Wildwood Dancing (Wildwood, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Wildwood Dancing</a>.<br /><br />George has written two sequels, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7199667.Princess_of_Glass__Princess___2_" title="Princess of Glass (Princess, #2) by Jessica Day George" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess of Glass</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12873027.Princess_of_the_Silver_Woods__Princess___3_" title="Princess of the Silver Woods (Princess, #3) by Jessica Day George" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess of the Silver Woods</a>, which continue the series with two of the younger princesses as main characters, and also weave in themes and elements from other fairy tales (Cinderella and Little Red Riding Hood, respectively). I actually consider both of these sequels stronger works than this first book in the series, primarily because of the greater creativity in their plots. If you or your child enjoys <i>Princess of the Midnight Ball</i>, it’s worth continuing with the series.<br /><br /><b>Initial thoughts:</b> There are YA books that are detailed and complex enough for adults to enjoy, and then there are those that are so simply told that they truly are just for the kids. This, I think, is one of the latter. <br /><br />Somehow three different novelizations of <i>The Twelve Dancing Princesses</i> have come my way in the last three or four months: this book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8428195.Entwined" title="Entwined by Heather Dixon" rel="nofollow noopener">Entwined</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13929.Wildwood_Dancing__Wildwood___1_" title="Wildwood Dancing (Wildwood, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Wildwood Dancing</a>. (None of them is perfect, but I liked <i>Wildwood Dancing</i> the best.) <i>Midnight Ball</i> will appeal mostly to girls in the 10-16 age range, I think. The writing is on the simplistic side. It was a pleasant, unobjectionable read and a fairly straightforward retelling of the original fairy tale. To put it another way, it felt very middle school-ish. Which is fine if you're 13.<br /><br />ETA: This book and my review just resurfaced in the comment thread, and I've been thinking again about this one and <i>Wildwood Dancing.</i> It's worth mentioning that I just increased my rating of <i>Wildwood</i> to 5 stars, and one year after reading <i>Princess of the Midnight Ball,</i> I have absolutely no recollection of the plot of this book, or how it's distinguishable from multiple other retellings of the twelve dancing princesses fairy tale. None. That doesn't mean it's a bad book, just that, for me, it was completely forgettable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12516122910134107341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42539322?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara" href="/user/show/1876075-cara">Cara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cara by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1884487-ash">Ash</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=awesome-covers">awesome-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42539322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2091104284271320704">I couldn't fall asleep one night and without even realizing it I was so caught up and enchanted by the story it was six in the morning when I finished the book.<br/><br/>This is a retelling but I'm not familiar with the original tale, so I can't say how close it is to the original. It stands on it's own though and you don't need any prior knowledge of the story to enjoy it.<br/><br/>The story starts out with our hero Galen (great name by the way) coming back from a war that he and his fellow soldiers have been figh</span>
  <span id="freeText2091104284271320704" style="display:none">I couldn't fall asleep one night and without even realizing it I was so caught up and enchanted by the story it was six in the morning when I finished the book.<br /><br />This is a retelling but I'm not familiar with the original tale, so I can't say how close it is to the original. It stands on it's own though and you don't need any prior knowledge of the story to enjoy it.<br /><br />The story starts out with our hero Galen (great name by the way) coming back from a war that he and his fellow soldiers have been fighting in for twelve years. At eighteen he has seen more tragedy and bloodshed than most have in their lives. Despite and because of all this he is such a lovable character. I won't go into detail but eventually his path crosses with the beloved twelve princesses of Westfalin (what would be considered Germany today most probably).<br /><br />There is a mystery surrounding the twelve princesses, for some reason their dancing slippers our all worn through every third night. No one sees where they go and can't seem to explain why this happens. The princesses: Rose, Lily, Jonquil, Hyacinth, Violet, Poppy, Daisy, Lilac, Iris, Orchid, Pansy, and Petunia (all named after flowers obviously) have to dance to serve a debt but they can't tell anybody. <br /><br />I did have trouble keeping up with which sister was which, but other than that the story flowed well. My sister who recommended it to me said that the beginning was slow going to her, but I thought the story had enough going on to keep the reader engaged. I can't say how much I loved the Galen character (too bad he isn't real and in reality I don't think there could be, but a girl can dream...) This enchanting, romantic, adventurous tale of Rose and Galen is a must read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2091104284271320704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

My issue is I had thought it would be a darker little tale then it was.<br/><br/>So I had an interest in this story. I read two books about it.   <span id="freeText2353853093725433496" style="display:none">He smiled his cold smile. "Keeping one's hands clean – maintaining one's innocence. Is that not the human way?”<br />― Jessica Day George, Princess of the Midnight Ball<br /><br />DNF.<br /><br /><br />I gave it a three even though I did not read to the end. My issue is I had thought it would be a darker little tale then it was.<br /><br />So I had an interest in this story. I read two books about it. This and one called Entwined.<br /><br />My issue with this one is it is really slow moving and felt very YA. Plus, I read a good deal in and nothing much had happened. I found there was not really alot going on, not at least when I stopped reading which was over 50 pages in.<br /><br />Not having read the book in its entirety I do not know whether it picked up but I got a bit impatient with this one.<br /><br /> I really wanted a dark adult book that retold this story and this was a slow moving YA that may have become darker but I just lacked the determination top keep going.<br /><br />I did enjoy the other one a bit more. My feeling is the story in and of itself is so fascinating but it IS dark and I thought it might be fun reading a few remakes.<br /><br />I have found though that the more remakes I read the less I like. I read a remake of Rebecca..a YA version and did not really love that one either so I suppose I may just not be the target audience.<br /><br />Check out the cover art on this one though..awesome!</span>

    <a title="Gkeller123" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1108857-gkeller123"><img alt="Gkeller123" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/43366855?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gkeller123" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gkeller123" href="/user/show/1108857-gkeller123">Gkeller123</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43366855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5906741446256345568">I bought this book yesterday at work, and was excited to start it. I had some time in the evening and read a few pages. When I woke early this morning and couldn't get back to sleep, I decided to read for a while. I couldn't stop until I had finished the WHOLE THING! I loved it. I have read other variations on the 12 dancing princesses, but this one had different twist and turns that made it so much different (and better!). </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2449450079" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2449450079" />
    <a title="enqi ☁️✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41427900-enqi"><img alt="enqi ☁️✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604082105p2/41427900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2449450079?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="enqi ☁️✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="enqi ☁️✨" href="/user/show/41427900-enqi">enqi ☁️✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10714386-princess-of-the-midnight-ball">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2449450079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13633241412489370203"><i> princess of the midnight ball </i> is a classic take on the well-known fairy tale of the <i> Twelve Dancing Princesses </i>, but decidedly much darker. this version of the story involves an ancient curse passed down to the princesses from their foolish mother and the mysterious deaths of the several princes who try to solve the mystery. its plot, however, doesn't really veer into unexpected territory, which meant that it was mostly just a very fleshed out version of the original fairy tale, albeit with so</span>
  <span id="freeText13633241412489370203" style="display:none"><i> princess of the midnight ball </i> is a classic take on the well-known fairy tale of the <i> Twelve Dancing Princesses </i>, but decidedly much darker. this version of the story involves an ancient curse passed down to the princesses from their foolish mother and the mysterious deaths of the several princes who try to solve the mystery. its plot, however, doesn't really veer into unexpected territory, which meant that it was mostly just a very fleshed out version of the original fairy tale, albeit with some minor twists.<br /><br />the characters were extremely underdeveloped and therefore a huge meh for me. the romance lacked passion and believability. i couldn't keep track of the princesses and their names, couldn't care less about Galen (more on that later) or Rose or their romance, and basically i think the only character in this story i remotely cared about was Gregor, the princesses' father. in the prologue, the villain of this book, a powerful dark magician, described him as fat and foolish and horrible but he ISN'T. he tries his best to be a good father and he actually would die for his daughters in an instant and he protects them at all costs and that's beautiful. #dadgoals <br /><br />okay anyway moving on, Galen actually put me off because he's obviously the white knight of the story and he's too perfect and never makes a single mistake idk?? i mean somehow when problems occur he thinks of a solution in like three minutes. and also he's supposed to be a Gentleman who is Gallant and Chivalrous, blah blah, but i think this just made his character really bland and boring. *it's probably a personal preference so take this with a pinch of salt.<br /><br />i don't really have much to say in this review because i don't really care about the book like it made me feel absolutely nothing and i skimmed at some points. however, i will admit that jessica day george has much talent in writing. her settings were descriptive and the fairytale backdrop felt almost magical to me. i did like another book of hers called <i> Sun and Moon, Ice and Snow </i>, so maybe it's just that i couldn't connect to the characters in this one. <br /><br />one more thing worth mentioning is Galen's unusual aptitude for knitting, and knitting plays quite an important role in this book. also, the author wrote this with influences from German (language, etc) and i found that quite interesting because i didn't associate Germany with the original fairy tale.<br /><br /><blockquote> <b> <i> "Just you remember: when you make a deal with them as lives below, there’s always a hidden price.” </i> </b> </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="13633241412489370203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1516924535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1516924535" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475352701p2/45261627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1516924535?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=a-fine-romance">a-fine-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=almost-gothic-in-a-natural-way">almost-gothic-in-a-natural-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=because-magic">because-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=because-marriage">because-marriage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=because-princesses">because-princesses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=gothic-fairytales">gothic-fairytales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=super-siblings">super-siblings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1516924535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16595995444832980330">The Ionian continent has been devastated by the ten-year war between the kingdoms of Westfalin and Analousia, which ended with Westfalin barely victorious, famine, a depressed economy, and thousands upon untold thousands of deaths.<br/><br/>Galen is a young veteran who lost his father, mother, and little sister during the war. He finds employment at the royal residence in Westfalin’s capitol, one of many men tending the late Queen’s massive, impractical flower garden. There he meets the twelve princesses,</span>
  <span id="freeText16595995444832980330" style="display:none">The Ionian continent has been devastated by the ten-year war between the kingdoms of Westfalin and Analousia, which ended with Westfalin barely victorious, famine, a depressed economy, and thousands upon untold thousands of deaths.<br><br>Galen is a young veteran who lost his father, mother, and little sister during the war. He finds employment at the royal residence in Westfalin’s capitol, one of many men tending the late Queen’s massive, impractical flower garden. There he meets the twelve princesses, secretive girls suffering under a curse...or are they the ones doing the cursing?<br><br>Rose, the King’s eldest daughter, likes Galen right away. But when he offers to solve her mystery, she’s dismayed. Many young men before him have tried to solve the curse. They were all princes, and all of them met wretched fates…<br><br>There’s an evil underground, just waiting until its descendants are human enough to walk abroad in sunlight.<br><br><b>Content Advisory</b><br><i>Violence</i>: A guy stabs a humanoid monster with a silver stake. Someone is knocked out, tied up, and imprisoned in a wardrobe. A little kid is bullied and forcibly interrogated by a crew of grown men while her father and sisters are absent. A woman is threatened with hanging. Characters frequently discuss the people they lost in the war and the pain they still feel.<br><br><i>Sex</i>: At the beginning, we hear a storyteller spin the tale of four sisters who were locked in a tower to protect them from evil influences, only for all four girls to be impregnated by the King Under Stone (in other news, the King Under Stone is Zeus). No details given.<br><br>One of the princes is supposedly given to making suggestive comments, but none of his (or anyone else’s) actual dialogue is remotely risqué.<br><br>Galen and Rose kiss exactly once. <br><br><i>Language</i>: None.<br><br><i>Substance Abuse</i>: None that I remember.<br><br><i>Nightmare Fuel</i>: The King Under Stone and most of his court look human, if rather pasty and elongated and generally Tim Burton-ish. But after centuries of living within the magical confines of their underworld, they can no longer go aboveground. The King’s sons are half-human and can endure fresh air, but like vampires and Uruk-hai, they cannot withstand sunlight. <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Under Stone is obsessed with marrying the princesses to his sons because ¾ humans would be able to survive aboveground and take over the kingdoms of Ionia. He also wants these weddings ASAP, apparently unwilling to wait for little Pansy and Petunia to at least hit puberty. Eek <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br><i>Politics and Religion</i>: The palace at Bruch becomes a battleground between kind Bishop Schelker and corrupt Bishop Angier. Angier is convinced that someone in the royal household is practicing black magic; Schelker, who baptized and catechized the princesses, knows that they are not the cause of these frightening events. Angier places the whole kingdom of Westfalin under Interdiction (no sacraments) until the “witch” is found, causing riots. Crosses, silver, and various folk remedies are all employed against the King Under Stone and his minions.<br><br><b>Conclusions</b><br>In <i>Princess of the Midnight Ball</i>, Jessica Day George does a superb job creating a tangible, richly atmospheric fantasy land very close to nineteenth-century Germany, conveying a sense of pleasant history, current hard times, and growing unrest. “The Twelve Dancing Princesses” is a rather strange tale, and George is the only author of a retelling whom I’ve really seen tackle how the sisters’ vanishing act would disturb the people of the kingdom. <br><br>I noticed in <i>Sun and Moon, Ice and Snow</i> that George seems fascinated with handicrafts (indeed, this book ends with instructions on how to knit the shawls and scarves described in the novel). Here, it serves the story well indeed. Knitting and cooking soup have a way of making characters grounded and real, no matter how outlandish their surroundings and stories may be. <br><br>Rose is mostly a noble character, whose main focus is on causing as little damage as she can. She’s not perfect—her lack of concern when the first several suitors die is disconcerting, to say the least. They were obnoxious, granted, but they were still human beings and they mattered to someone. But given Rose’s situation, it makes sense that she does not get attached to people easily. She’s a practical, level-headed leader, and the younger princesses could not ask for a better older sister. <br><br>Galen is shrewd and charming. The book spends equal time looking through his eyes and Rose’s, which gives him a lot more depth than the average love interest in a fairytale retelling. I loved his bravery and his attitude—after living through the war that killed his entire family, he has no time for the King Under Stone’s nonsense. I also loved his interactions with the little girls and his sweet knitting skills. He’s as swoon-worthy as Eugenides of Eddis and George Cooper, and twice as wholesome. He’s one for the Heroic Heartthrob Hall of Fame.<br><br>The King Under Stone is suitably terrifying, although I feel like a lot of questions remain about him. That said, this is the first book in a series...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1544498091ra/26726122.gif" width="500" height="358" alt="I am patient. I can wait" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a gently paced story that steeps the reader in a world of wool clothing, cold evenings, soup for supper, and slowly building dread. The characters are worth cheering for, and reading more about. There’s daring escapes, romance, chills, and humor. Highly recommended. <i>Princess of Glass</i> is in transit to my library and I can’t wait. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16595995444832980330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1154879608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11494308217481395692">Felt just like the fairytales I grew up on. Maybe not my favorite book as far as YA or romance, but it was still spellbinding from first page to last, there's just something special about the storytelling that made me feel as if I were reliving the old illustrated collection I grew up on. I would get this book for anyone that loves fairytales in a heartbeat.</span>

    <div class="elementListBrownSeparator"></div>



  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_232598873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/232598873" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/232598873?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2016">read2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=3stars">3stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232598873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12918051828056252323"><blockquote>
  <i>“And all because of some shoes,” Galen murmured as they hurried away.<br/>“What?” Ulrike had to trot to keep up with him.<br/>“This all began because of their shoes being worn out night after night,” he said. He had fallen into an easy quick-march pace. He put an arm around his cousin’s waist to help her along.<br/>“If someone could just figure out what they do every night.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Princess of the Midnight Ball is a retelling of the old favourite fairy-tale of The Twelve Dancing Princesses and it is just lovely…<b>LO</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12918051828056252323" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“And all because of some shoes,” Galen murmured as they hurried away.<br />“What?” Ulrike had to trot to keep up with him.<br />“This all began because of their shoes being worn out night after night,” he said. He had fallen into an easy quick-march pace. He put an arm around his cousin’s waist to help her along.<br />“If someone could just figure out what they do every night.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Princess of the Midnight Ball is a retelling of the old favourite fairy-tale of The Twelve Dancing Princesses and it is just lovely…<b>LOVELY!!!</b> A book that makes you happy, holds your hand, offers you a warm smile and a friendly embrace. I made a lot of contented sighing noises while reading this. <br /><br /><br />It is a nice, easy read. It is not too taxing on the mind, not too heavy on the heart… everything just happens at a gentle pace. The retelling focuses on Galen: a soldier that has just returned from war, and is offered a position working in the Queen’s garden with his only living relative. Here Galen meets the twelve princesses and in particular, the story focuses on Rose, the eldest princess. Galen and Rose have a really sweet relationship. They instantly like each other and there follows some gentle flirting and teasing….and cue much girlish sighing on my part.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Well Your Highness, I know that I am indeed handsome, but I can hardly be blamed if my good looks overcame you so strongly that you fainted,” he said, striking a pose. He had butterflies in his stomach, wondering if he was taking the teasing too far.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />However there is mystery in the palace! New dancing slippers are required each day keeping the King’s cobbler very busy and tongues wagging in the kingdom. Despite being locked into their rooms at night with maids and guards keeping vigil each of the twelve princesses appear each morning with worn out dancing slippers… where do the girls go to??? The princesses become weaker and sickly, yet still each morning they appear with worn out slippers??? Who is forcing them to dance against their will?? What witchcraft could it be??? Are they all cursed??? Or are they the ones doing the cursing???<br /><br /><br />Noble princes are sent to find out and are promised hands in marriage and kingship if they solve the mystery… but to no avail and mysteriously each of these princes soon die after returning to their own lands.<br /><br /><br />It is up to our brave soldier-cum-gardener Galen to figure out the mystery, break the spell and banish the evil doers….<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“He was the stuff of nightmares, the stuff of campfire tales. A magician so steeped in evil that he had ceased to be human, transforming himself and his most devout followers into something other: immortal and monstrous. According to legend, centuries ago every country on the continent of Ionia had risen up against him and cast him into an underground prison. He was too powerful to be destroyed completely, and trapping him in a sunless realm with only his followers to rule over had been the only solution. An army of white witches had been gathered to do the deed, and the effort had cost many of them their lives”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />Don’t you love a good fairy-tale?????? This was just <i>
  <b>so</b>
</i> cute!!!!!!!!! SO CUTE!!!!!!!!!! Ok so there wasn’t exactly great character development outside of Galen and Rose…. It was like Princess Rose and eleven other florally named princesses who all merged together into one character… but I did not mind! I enjoyed the slow-pacing. I enjoyed the romance, the intrigue, the mystery… <br /><br />Sometimes we need life to go at a slower pace. <br />We need to escape the harshness of the real world and I found my escape here in the pages of this book. <br /><u>Did it change my life?<br />Blow me away? <br />Make me feel all the feels???</u> <br />…No it didn’t. But some times that is <i>
  <b>not</b>
</i> the point!!! <br /><br /><b>This book made me smile. It made me happy. It gave me good feelings. It left me with a sense of contentment…</b> <br />And sometimes all we want from life is that <i>
  <b>happily ever after…</b>
</i><br /><br />Read this if you want something gentle, if you are tired, if you are ill… It will restore your soul and gently cradle you between its loving pages.<br /><br /><br /><b>Three stars.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Their fingers touched when she took it from him, and they stayed that way for a moment, hands together, the rose cradled between them.”</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12918051828056252323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97845811" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97845811" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97845811?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Shannon Hale</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=children-s-middle-school">children-s-middle-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97845811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer510244294588136744"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3697927.Princess_of_the_Midnight_Ball' title='Princess of the Midnight Ball by Jessica Day George' rel='nofollow noopener'>Princess of the Midnight Ball</a> is an utterly inoffensive retelling of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13012.Brothers_Grimm' title='Brothers Grimm' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brothers Grimm</a>'s fairy tale <i>Twelve Dancing Princesses</i>. No gore, no violence here, suitable for pretty much any age.<br/><br/>The premise is straight forward - the King of Westfalin's 12 daughters nightly wear out their dancing slippers. Several princes attempt to uncover the princesses' secret for a reward of inheriting the Kingdom, but fail. Only 19-year old Galen - an ex-soldier/now gardener - succeeds in finding out the truth with the</span>
  <span id="freeText510244294588136744" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3697927.Princess_of_the_Midnight_Ball" title="Princess of the Midnight Ball by Jessica Day George" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess of the Midnight Ball</a> is an utterly inoffensive retelling of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13012.Brothers_Grimm" title="Brothers Grimm" rel="nofollow noopener">Brothers Grimm</a>'s fairy tale <i>Twelve Dancing Princesses</i>. No gore, no violence here, suitable for pretty much any age.<br /><br />The premise is straight forward - the King of Westfalin's 12 daughters nightly wear out their dancing slippers. Several princes attempt to uncover the princesses' secret for a reward of inheriting the Kingdom, but fail. Only 19-year old Galen - an ex-soldier/now gardener - succeeds in finding out the truth with the help of an invisibility cloak and some magical wool.<br /><br />I am not familiar with the original tale, so it's hard to tell how much the author has expanded on it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3697927.Princess_of_the_Midnight_Ball" title="Princess of the Midnight Ball by Jessica Day George" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess of the Midnight Ball</a> is a nicely written story with an interesting setting and likable characters. Galen is certainly a peculiar hero with a penchant for knitting (yeah, I know, not necessarily a turn-on for me either) and princesses are mostly interesting too, especially those who are developed better. <br /><br />The main weakness of the story IMO is that the magic is a bit shaky - it is unexplained why Galen knows how to do certain things. <br /><br />I can't say there is anything remarkable or of a wow quality here - no spectacular writing or characterization or mythology, but overall the novel is a cute, light, engaging read. I will probably read more retellings by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/359109.Jessica_Day_George" title="Jessica Day George" rel="nofollow noopener">Jessica Day George</a>, whenever mood calls for something like it. As for the original fairy tale, I'd like to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier" title="Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliet Marillier</a>'s version - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13929.Wildwood_Dancing__Wildwood___1_" title="Wildwood Dancing (Wildwood, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Wildwood Dancing</a> or, gasp, an erotic version <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1519385.The_Twelve_Dancing_Princesses" title="The Twelve Dancing Princesses by Nancy Madore" rel="nofollow noopener">The Twelve Dancing Princesses</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/365496.Nancy_Madore" title="Nancy Madore" rel="nofollow noopener">Nancy Madore</a>. Maybe these two put some new, interesting spin on it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="510244294588136744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099959163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17632614618071829454"><blockquote>
  <b>5 out of 10</b>
</blockquote><br/><a href='http://www.livelib.ru/review/516469' rel='nofollow noopener'>ревью на русском/review in russian</a><br/><br/><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br/><a href='ww.youtube.com/watch?v=Ne-jgxiFCPM' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pianochocolate – Waltz</a><br/><a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rwUkE_A5A1c' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cassidy Ladden – Shine</a><br/><a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Jg5RMc8evzo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Yuriko Nakamura – Flower </a><br/><br/>Well, I don’t know what to say. I thought it would be a true retelling for young adult auditory but this is an extended version of the old Grimm’s tale for middle grade people or even children.<br/><br/>The plot is more than close to the original story about twelve princesses. <br/><br/>The book is good but the idea and its execution were shamelessly stolen. Okay, it's a retelling, </span>
  <span id="freeText17632614618071829454" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>5 out of 10</b>
</blockquote><br /><a href="http://www.livelib.ru/review/516469" rel="nofollow noopener">ревью на русском/review in russian</a><br /><br /><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br /><a href="ww.youtube.com/watch?v=Ne-jgxiFCPM" rel="nofollow noopener">Pianochocolate – Waltz</a><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rwUkE_A5A1c" rel="nofollow noopener">Cassidy Ladden – Shine</a><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Jg5RMc8evzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Yuriko Nakamura – Flower </a><br /><br />Well, I don’t know what to say. I thought it would be a true retelling for young adult auditory but this is an extended version of the old Grimm’s tale for middle grade people or even children.<br /><br />The plot is more than close to the original story about twelve princesses. <br /><br />The book is good but the idea and its execution were shamelessly stolen. Okay, it's a retelling, usually this is normal. But only if you take an idea and develop it in your own way. When you transform 30-pages-story into a 280-pages-one (a lot of dialogues and inner monologues make wonders) by pouring water between the lines, and then sign the result with your name... that smells like plagiarism. Or laziness. <br /> <br />I was waiting for unexpected twists, for some underground-orgies, court intrigues and revolutions… even a mere good romance could save the story for me. But all I’ve a got was a chip rainbow.<br /><br />The book is well-written, it fairytale-stuff looks nice, but the author did miss with her audience. The plot is too simple, clean and steady for ya-guys, there are no blood, real kisses or strong language. So why YA?<br /> <br />For me the book was a waste of time. But juveniles would love it, I guess. <br /><br /><b>The Princesses of Westfalin (Принцессы Вестафалина):</b><br /><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1099959163" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess of the Midnight Ball (Принцесса полночного бала)</a> #1/3<br />— Princess of Glass (Принцесса стекла) #2/3<br />— Princess of the Silver Woods (Принцесса серебряных лесов) #3/3</blockquote><br /></span>

    <a title="Isabel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5086874-isabel"><img alt="Isabel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497661821p2/5086874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164774163?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isabel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isabel" href="/user/show/5086874-isabel">Isabel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781599904559" href="/book/show/7151460-princess-of-the-midnight-ball">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer164774163&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164774163" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2653013510728102211">So, unfortunately I promised a few people that I would write a review on this book (I mean, maybe one... or two...) so here's my best attempt at writing one: (note: I am not particularly good at writing thoughtful, lengthy reviews)<br/><br/>To be quite frank, upon finishing <i>Princess of the Midnight Ball</i> I felt deeply annoyed at myself for ever having picked up this book -- and having it sit in the corner of my room, making me feel guilty, for almost eight months. At times this book showed some potential (</span>
  <span id="freeText2653013510728102211" style="display:none">So, unfortunately I promised a few people that I would write a review on this book (I mean, maybe one... or two...) so here's my best attempt at writing one: (note: I am not particularly good at writing thoughtful, lengthy reviews)<br /><br />To be quite frank, upon finishing <i>Princess of the Midnight Ball</i> I felt deeply annoyed at myself for ever having picked up this book -- and having it sit in the corner of my room, making me feel guilty, for almost eight months. At times this book showed some potential (most definitely not as a YA book, however) but the plot was so askew and the characters -- especially Galen and Rose, two of the most annoying POVs ever -- were cliche and didn't have the slightest depth. I got so bored mid-way through the book, and already felt like it should have ended by then even though the story is already <i>very</i> short at 272 pages. There were lots of problems with the story itself, and it lacked much excitement and most definitely a good romance. Galen and Rose were such an annoying pair and their feelings for each other didn't seem real to me; I honestly didn't much care whether their "relationship" would work out in the end or not. And -- I suppose this is a spoiler, but it was so pathetically lame that I don't think it really matters if you read on -- Heinrich returning to Lily in the end (during Galen and Rose's WEDDING, wow) made me groan and actually put down the book for a few minutes. The King Under Stone was a terrible villain, and Rose's story began to get quite tiresome to me. There were many loopholes in the plot, too -- for one, why did the king only realize that the princesses wore out their dancing slippers every third night after they had already been doing it for YEARS? And why did Angier still seem completely oblivious to what was going on with the princesses even after gaining possession of Queen Maude's diary?<br /><br />Despite its many faults, I do believe that if I had picked up <i>Princess of the Midnight Ball</i> at an earlier age I might have enjoyed it more. Unfortunately, though, I don't think I'll be giving any of Jessica Day George's other books a shot for a while now. Perhaps they just aren't my thing. I also know how much thought and hard work goes into writing a book like this, and I appreciate that fully -- this is purely my opinion, not meant to offend anybody. I did enjoy some of the humor in this book, and some parts of it were pleasurable. But I must say I'm glad to have finally gotten it over with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2653013510728102211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It introduced me to fairytale retellings, it revitalized my love of writing, it inspired me in all the best ways and stuck with me forever. To this day I'm still always a little surprised with 12DP retellings don't involve a gardener. xD <br /><br />There's just so much to love about this book, okay? Supportive sisters, adorable romance, banter, sass, intrigue, it's just so good, ahh! The plot is engaging, the characters are wonderful, the setting is fascinating, and really, it's just the best classic Twelve Dancing Princesses retelling I've read. It holds a special place in my heart. <br /><br />Five stars from me.</span>

<div id="review_156585467" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156585467" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=multiple-viewpoints">multiple-viewpoints</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156585467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4848726304088021074">Princess of the Midnight Ball is a retelling of the Twelve Dancing Princesses story. Maybe I haven't looked closely enough, but one rarely sees this particular story get retold. Probably because it requires a big cast of characters. Yes, there are indeed twelve dancing princesses here, and George tries valiantly to give them all personality, but there's only so much an author can do in 270 pages. That said, the featured princesses were all interesting enough that it didn't bother me that some (D</span>
  <span id="freeText4848726304088021074" style="display:none">Princess of the Midnight Ball is a retelling of the Twelve Dancing Princesses story. Maybe I haven't looked closely enough, but one rarely sees this particular story get retold. Probably because it requires a big cast of characters. Yes, there are indeed twelve dancing princesses here, and George tries valiantly to give them all personality, but there's only so much an author can do in 270 pages. That said, the featured princesses were all interesting enough that it didn't bother me that some (Daisy, for example) weren't given much substance. I was also thoroughly charmed by our hero, Galen. I will cheerfully admit that I decided to read this book because Galen is a knitter. And his knitting is not only an integral part of the character, it's an integral part of the plot. <br /><br />The story itself is mostly a straight-forward retelling of the original. Mostly. The last bit of the book is taken up largely with unnecessary complications that result mostly from Galen, who before had always been clever and wise, acting like a bit of an idiot. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes, Galen, you may indeed be hiding behind a cloak of invisibility that is your only protection from the powerful king of the underworld, but have a drink anyways! Or a few! And then dance with one of the princesses, making sure you draw everybody's attention! Great idea! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also largely unnecessary is the plot thread about the princesses being considered witches.<br /><br />And yet, I still enjoyed the book. There's something to be said for a retelling that doesn't mess too much with the source material. And there's something to be said for a sweet and simple fantasy with a nice romance. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4848726304088021074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Paige  Bookdragon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15550986-paige-bookdragon"><img alt="Paige  Bookdragon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570121828p2/15550986.jpg" /></a>

The author made me care about the plight of the princesses as they danced nightly to fulfill the promise their mother made to the evil Under Stone. Along came our clever hero. Even though I knew the tale Jessica George skillfully wove in new characters and plot twists that kept me intrigued. I am sure to read the next book in this series sometime soon.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1045577064" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1045577064" />
    <a title="Olga Godim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim"><img alt="Olga Godim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442639299p2/7438487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1045577064?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olga Godim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olga Godim" href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim">Olga Godim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7438487-olga-godim?shelf=fantasy-scifi">fantasy-scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1045577064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3225124048107243618">A retelling of <i>The Twelve Dancing Princesses</i>, this charming novel for early teens is also good for a grownup reader. Unlike the original fairy tale, in this story, the princesses don’t want to dance at the Midnight Ball every night but they have no choice: they are under a curse by an evil sorcerer. Moreover, the curse makes it impossible for them to tell anyone or to ask for help. <br/>The heroes of this story, the eldest princess, eighteen-year-old Rose, and a former soldier, nineteen-year-old Gale</span>
  <span id="freeText3225124048107243618" style="display:none">A retelling of <i>The Twelve Dancing Princesses</i>, this charming novel for early teens is also good for a grownup reader. Unlike the original fairy tale, in this story, the princesses don’t want to dance at the Midnight Ball every night but they have no choice: they are under a curse by an evil sorcerer. Moreover, the curse makes it impossible for them to tell anyone or to ask for help. <br />The heroes of this story, the eldest princess, eighteen-year-old Rose, and a former soldier, nineteen-year-old Galen, fall in love, of course, while Galen tries to figure out Rose’s secret and how to help her and her sisters. The plot follows the source pretty closely, but as always with fairy tales, the characters are much better developed.<br />Rose, as the oldest, feels responsible for her younger sisters. She is a delightful girl, beautiful inside and out. She would do anything to break the spell hanging over her sisters’ heads, but there is nothing she can do until Galen comes along. <br />A son of a soldier, Galen grew up with the army. He fought in battles since he was fourteen. At nineteen, he is a veteran. Fortunately, the long war is finally over, and he finds a job as a gardener in the king’s gardens. He is a practical guy, with no illusions but lots of compassion. He is brave. He sees that the princesses suffer and he longs to help. <br />It was a light, uncomplicated book. A little magic, a little teenage affection, and everything clean and sparkling, with no resemblance to anything even remotely related to real life. Even the writer’s attempts to indulge in political machinations are simplified, while she builds her tension and ups the stakes for the protagonists. <br />The only complaint I have is that the author named all twelve princesses, all by different flower names, and I couldn’t distinguish between them, neither names nor ages, no matter how much I tried. Otherwise, it was a book to rest your soul after all the battles and flawed heroes of modern adult fantasy. <br />I must be sliding back into childhood: I’m developing a taste for children’s fantasy, and Ms. George is helping me. I already read a couple of her other books and I’m going to read more. They make me happy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3225124048107243618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/713340890" />
    <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired"><img alt="Rashika (is tired)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476647072p2/8492956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/713340890?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rashika (is tired)" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired">Rashika (is tired)</a>
      </span>

          added it




          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rashika (is tired) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5387491-mel-daily-prophecy">Mel (Daily Prophecy)</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=cute-romance">cute-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=totally-worth-it">totally-worth-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=have-not-rated">have-not-rated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=cute-love-interests">cute-love-interests</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer713340890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17287818248234965462">This is going to be a real quick overview since I don't have much time right now but I cannot hold in all my feels for this book. <br/><br/>This is a dark re-telling but at the same time it's kind of fluffy. It has that fairy tale feel to it (since well it is a re-telling) so not everything will always line up but somehow this story still charmed me to no ends.<br/><br/>The romance could be seen as insta, no doubt, but it didn't bother me. I enjoyed it if only I wished there was a little more development going on b</span>
  <span id="freeText17287818248234965462" style="display:none">This is going to be a real quick overview since I don't have much time right now but I cannot hold in all my feels for this book. <br /><br />This is a dark re-telling but at the same time it's kind of fluffy. It has that fairy tale feel to it (since well it is a re-telling) so not everything will always line up but somehow this story still charmed me to no ends.<br /><br />The romance could be seen as insta, no doubt, but it didn't bother me. I enjoyed it if only I wished there was a little more development going on but that's what I mean when I say this is kind of fluffy. There are some things that are done in a very fairy-taleish way but it works.<br /><br />I mean with a soldier turned gardner who is to save the day with his epic knitting skills, how can you not help but be charmed? <br /><br />The characters, were so adorable too! Both Rose and Galen are mature but at the same time, they seem innocent too in this childish way that is just so hard to put into words. <br /><br />The secondary characters were SO SO FUN. They made this book so much more funner to read.<br /><br />The plot, I'd say could use a little more polishing but at the end of the day, this was a highly entertaining read and I couldn't help but be charmed.<br /><br />This book in general, as you can conclude from my overview, is somewhat hard for me to describe or explain because it seems almost contradictory. It's dark, no doubt, with it's setting and just the general atmosphere of the book but at the same time, it'll make you smile and giggle and just leave you with a huge smile on your face, the kind you'd get from reading a fluffy book.<br /><br />It's a quick read too so if you're not sure about it, I'd still tell you to give it a shot because you might just end up liking it!<br /><br />With all that said, I have no idea what to rate this book so I am just going to leave it as it is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17287818248234965462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230439087" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5641932160209993652">While I wouldn't normally pick up a fantasy/fairytale book (as fantasy isn't my favorite genre), Princess of the Midnight Ball was highly recommended to my by a friend. After reading the book, I am glad I took her advice to get a copy! <br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed this sweet fairytale! It made for a very easy read and the story plot captivated me. Galen was easy to grow to like as the hero of this tale. I was surprised that most often the story was written from his POV (point of view) and not Princess R</span>
  <span id="freeText5641932160209993652" style="display:none">While I wouldn't normally pick up a fantasy/fairytale book (as fantasy isn't my favorite genre), Princess of the Midnight Ball was highly recommended to my by a friend. After reading the book, I am glad I took her advice to get a copy! <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this sweet fairytale! It made for a very easy read and the story plot captivated me. Galen was easy to grow to like as the hero of this tale. I was surprised that most often the story was written from his POV (point of view) and not Princess Rose, but it wasn't a bad surprise---Jessica wove together the entire story wonderfully well. And I enjoyed reading it from a guy's POV. <br /><br />All in all, a delightful fairytale that young teens and adults will both be sure to enjoy. It's a very light, quick, easy read. There is a bit of 'magic' in the book, as the girls go to an 'underworld' of sorts, but the magic wasn't a very heavy part of the book. I look forward to reading the next book in the series!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_88097693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88097693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7256831247455729062">I don’t give four star ratings lightly, especially to young adult retellings of classic fairy tales. The stories are relatively well known and have been reworked and rewritten… the long and the short of it is that they have been done and done to death. Finding a fresh outlook is like finding a needle in a haystack. Jessica Day George’s Princess of the Midnight Ball is that needle. George fleshes out the back story and makes a few small changes to the original telling. The result is an enchanting</span>
  <span id="freeText7256831247455729062" style="display:none">I don’t give four star ratings lightly, especially to young adult retellings of classic fairy tales. The stories are relatively well known and have been reworked and rewritten… the long and the short of it is that they have been done and done to death. Finding a fresh outlook is like finding a needle in a haystack. Jessica Day George’s Princess of the Midnight Ball is that needle. George fleshes out the back story and makes a few small changes to the original telling. The result is an enchantingly fresh and original look at the classic fairy tale. <br /><br />One particularly notable aspect is that the story is told not by one of the princesses but from the perspective of battle weary soldier turned under gardener, Galen Werner. The Twelve Dancing Princesses is very much a girls story. I think shifting focus to the male character really helps the book by adding a sense of balance to an otherwise light and frilly fantasy.<br /><br />One of my favorite things about the book is that George doesn’t waste time giving each girl her moment. Twelve girls is a huge cast for a book with that doesn’t even number 300 pages. In fact, many retellings reduce the number of princesses in order simply the narrative. George opted instead to focus on a few of the princesses, making it easier to relate to her characters while remaining true to the story.<br /><br />The decision to make Galen a proficient knitter was inspired. Traditionally considered the past time of aging matriarchs I found his hobby an ingenious and creative tool by which to feature our hero’s personality. This isn’t the knight in shining armor, poised gallantly atop his noble steed. Again, George broke away from the familiar and fashioned something distinctly unique.<br /><br />Sweet, charming and heartfelt, Princess of the Midnight ball is not to be missed. Recommended to fans of A Curse Dark as Gold. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7256831247455729062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
